###begin article-title 0
The Secreted Metalloprotease ADAMTS20 Is Required for Melanoblast Survival
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Current address: Alba Therapeutics, Baltimore, Maryland, United States of America
###end p 1
###begin p 2
Conceived and designed the experiments: DS SA WP. Performed the experiments: DS LH RS MY. Analyzed the data: DS LH RS MY SA WP. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: DS LH RS MY WP. Wrote the paper: DS SA WP.
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 10 11 10 11 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 11 12 11 12 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</underline>
###xml 28 29 28 29 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</underline>
###xml 32 33 32 33 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</underline>
###xml 60 61 60 61 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</underline>
###xml 67 68 67 68 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</underline>
###xml 235 243 235 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 257 263 257 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">belted</italic>
###xml 265 267 265 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 429 437 429 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 534 542 534 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 593 596 593 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
###xml 725 730 725 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt</italic>
###xml 792 797 792 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt</italic>
###xml 924 929 924 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt</italic>
###xml 975 982 975 982 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 1003 1011 1003 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 1149 1157 1149 1157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 1240 1248 1240 1248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 1362 1368 1362 1368 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 1353 1368 1353 1368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt;Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 1385 1387 1385 1387 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sl</sup>
###xml 1375 1387 1375 1387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt;Kitl<sup>Sl</sup></italic>
###xml 1504 1512 1504 1512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1555 1562 1555 1562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1702 1708 1702 1708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts</italic>
###xml 269 273 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1390 1394 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
ADAMTS20 (Adisintegrin-like and metalloprotease domain with thrombospondin type-1 motifs) is a member of a family of secreted metalloproteases that can process a variety of extracellular matrix (ECM) components and secreted molecules. Adamts20 mutations in belted (bt) mice cause white spotting of the dorsal and ventral torso, indicative of defective neural crest (NC)-derived melanoblast development. The expression pattern of Adamts20 in dermal mesenchymal cells adjacent to migrating melanoblasts led us to initially propose that Adamts20 regulated melanoblast migration. However, using a Dct-LacZ transgene to track melanoblast development, we determined that melanoblasts were distributed normally in whole mount E12.5 bt/bt embryos, but were specifically reduced in the trunk of E13.5 bt/bt embryos due to a seven-fold higher rate of apoptosis. The melanoblast defect was exacerbated in newborn skin and embryos from bt/bt animals that were also haploinsufficient for Adamts9, a close homolog of Adamts20, indicating that these metalloproteases functionally overlap in melanoblast development. We identified two potential mechanisms by which Adamts20 may regulate melanoblast survival. First, skin explant cultures demonstrated that Adamts20 was required for melanoblasts to respond to soluble Kit ligand (sKitl). In support of this requirement, bt/bt;Kittm1Alf/+ and bt/bt;KitlSl/+ mice exhibited synergistically increased spotting. Second, ADAMTS20 cleaved the aggregating proteoglycan versican in vitro and was necessary for versican processing in vivo, raising the possibility that versican can participate in melanoblast development. These findings reveal previously unrecognized roles for Adamts proteases in cell survival and in mediating Kit signaling during melanoblast colonization of the skin. Our results have implications not only for understanding mechanisms of NC-derived melanoblast development but also provide insights on novel biological functions of secreted metalloproteases.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Author Summary
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 336 345 336 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20,</italic>
###xml 414 422 414 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 679 687 679 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 79 84 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 129 134 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 231 236 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 356 360 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Mice with black and white coat coloration patterns have long been favorites of mouse fanciers and geneticists alike. Analysis of mouse coat color mutants has yielded important insights into normal developmental pathways as well as human disease processes. In this study we have investigated how mutations in a secreted metalloprotease, Adamts20, result in mice with white belts in their lumbar region, even though Adamts20 is not expressed in the pigment producing cells. Our findings suggest that the belting pattern is due to a combination of increased pigment cell death, decreased pigment cell number in the trunk, and functional overlap of closely related metalloproteases. Adamts20 mutants have disrupted function of Kit, a protein that regulates pigment cell development, as well as alterations in the extracellular matrix that surrounds the pigment cells. These findings have implications both for our understanding of general mechanisms of pigment cell development as well as for new biological functions of secreted metalloproteases.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Introduction
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 0 3 0 3 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A d</underline>
###xml 19 20 19 20 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</underline>
###xml 23 24 23 24 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</underline>
###xml 44 45 44 45 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</underline>
###xml 51 52 51 52 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</underline>
###xml 205 206 205 206 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 206 207 206 207 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</underline>
###xml 218 219 218 219 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</underline>
###xml 222 223 222 223 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</underline>
###xml 299 302 299 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Apte1">[1]</xref>
###xml 303 306 303 306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Porter1">[2]</xref>
###xml 1087 1090 1087 1090 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Glasson1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1091 1094 1091 1094 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Stanton1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1343 1346 1343 1346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Levy1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1348 1351 1348 1351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Colige1">[8]</xref>
###xml 1352 1356 1352 1356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Tortorella1">[10]</xref>
###xml 864 869 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
A disintegrin-like and metalloprotease with thrombospondin type-1 motifs (ADAMTS) metalloproteases constitute a large family of 19 zinc-dependent proteolytic enzymes that are distantly related to both the Adisintegrin and metalloproteinase (ADAM) family, and to the matrix metalloproteinases (MMPs) [1],[2]. In contrast to the ADAM proteases that are membrane anchored, ADAMTS proteases are secreted; however, some may be considered as operational cell-surface proteases as they bind to the cell surface. Some ADAMTS proteases, such as ADAMTS10 (GeneID: 224697), ADAMTS13 (GeneID: 279028), and the procollagen amino-propeptidases (e.g. ADAMTS2), are highly specialized; others process a variety of substrates within the extracellular matrix (ECM), including chondroitin sulfate proteoglycans (CSPGs), such as aggrecan (GeneID: 11595) and versican (GeneID: 13003). Mouse models harboring mutations in ADAMTS family members have demonstrated the importance of these proteases during development. In some cases mutant phenotypes can be attributed to a failure to cleave specific substrates [3]-[7]. Mutation or dysregulation of ADAMTS proteases is associated with inherited and acquired pathologies including Ehlers-Danlos syndrome VIIC (OMIM#225410), thrombocytopenic purpura (OMIM#274150), Weill-Marchesani syndrome (OMIM#277600) and arthritis [5], [8]-[10].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 28 34 28 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts</italic>
###xml 86 92 86 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">belted</italic>
###xml 94 96 94 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 195 199 195 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mayer1">[11]</xref>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Schaible1">[13]</xref>
###xml 257 263 257 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">belted</italic>
###xml 266 270 266 270 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>
###xml 264 270 264 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Bei1</sup></italic>
###xml 274 278 274 278 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mri1</sup>
###xml 272 278 272 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Mri1</sup></italic>
###xml 284 286 284 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 371 379 371 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 436 440 436 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 681 685 681 685 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Lin1">[14]</xref>
###xml 686 690 686 690 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Silver1">[15]</xref>
###xml 74 79 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 288 293 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Among the animal mutants in Adamts proteases is a classical white-spotted mouse named belted (bt), so named because it contains white spots in the lumbar region creating the appearance of a belt [11]-[13]. Sequencing of three of the twelve known alleles of belted-btBei1, btMri1, and bt (Mouse Genome Informatics, MGI: 2660628)-revealed nonsense or missense mutations in Adamts20, thus implicating metalloproteases in skin pigmentation [12]. Analyses of white spotting mutants suggest that such phenotypes are often due to defective development of neural crest (NC)-derived melanoblasts that produce pigment of the integument (skin, hair, feathers, and scales), inner ear, and eye [14],[15].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 222 226 222 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Silver1">[15]</xref>
###xml 227 231 227 231 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Serbedzija1">[16]</xref>
###xml 568 571 568 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 576 580 576 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 705 709 705 709 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Cable1">[17]</xref>
###xml 710 714 710 714 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida1">[23]</xref>
###xml 716 719 716 719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 754 758 754 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 839 843 839 843 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-WehrleHaller1">[21]</xref>
###xml 845 849 845 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Matsui1">[24]</xref>
###xml 850 854 850 854 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida2">[26]</xref>
Melanoblasts develop from a subset of NC that emigrate from the neural tube and overlying ectoderm and migrate dorso-laterally relative to the neural tube through prospective dermal mesenchyme (embryonic day (E) 8.5-E9.5) [15],[16]. Subsequently, the melanoblasts differentiate and expand (E9.5-E13.5), migrate into the epidermis and hair follicle (E13.5-E15.5), and eventually produce melanin (E15.5-P0). Several molecules, including the receptor tyrosine kinase Kit (GeneID: 16590) and its ligand, Kit ligand (Kitl, GeneID: 17311), regulate melanoblast development. Kit and Kitl act throughout melanoblast development, with independent requirements for melanoblast survival, proliferation and migration [17]-[23]. Kit is expressed on melanoblasts, and Kitl is expressed in the dermis and in dermal mesenchymal condensations and papillae [21], [24]-[26].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 11 15 11 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 17 25 17 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 211 213 211 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 270 274 270 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 337 345 337 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 355 360 355 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gon-1</italic>
###xml 450 459 450 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C.elegans</italic>
###xml 459 463 459 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Blelloch1">[27]</xref>
###xml 464 468 464 468 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hesselson1">[29]</xref>
###xml 580 585 580 585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt</italic>
###xml 621 629 621 629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 800 807 800 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 855 860 855 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt</italic>
###xml 450 459 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C.elegans</span>
###xml 637 641 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Similar to Kitl, Adamts20 is expressed in dermal mesenchymal cells adjacent to and in advance of migrating melanoblasts throughout their development. This expression pattern led us to initially propose that the bt phenotype was caused by defective melanoblast migration [12]. This hypothesis was also based upon the observation that the Adamts20 ortholog Gon-1 (GeneID: 177850) is essential for gonadal morphogenesis and distal tip cell migration in C.elegans[27]-[29]. The current study tests our hypothesis by performing extensive characterization of melanoblast development in bt/bt embryos. Our findings suggest that Adamts20 mutant mice exhibit white spotting in a belted pattern due to a combination of regional variation of melanoblast number, increased apoptosis, and functional overlap with Adamts9 (GeneID: 101401). Furthermore, our analyses of bt/bt embryos indicate that defective Kit signaling and versican processing may explain the failure of melanoblasts to develop properly.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
Results
###end title 11
###begin title 12
###xml 48 54 48 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Belted</italic>
Genetic and Molecular Characterization of a New Belted Allele
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 179 188 179 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mayer1">[11]</xref>
###xml 195 199 195 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Schaible1">[13]</xref>
###xml 232 234 232 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 345 347 345 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 358 362 358 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hauschka1">[30]</xref>
###xml 363 367 363 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Lamoreux1">[31]</xref>
###xml 378 386 378 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 517 519 517 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 531 535 531 535 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>
###xml 529 537 529 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Bei1</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 585 587 585 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 650 652 650 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 694 696 694 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 736 738 736 738 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 734 738 734 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 16 20 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 520 524 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 538 542 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Adamts20 mutant mice exhibit white spotting in the lumbar region on both dorsal and ventral surfaces, frequently resulting in the appearance of a white belt in recessive animals (Figure 1A) [11]-[13]. For these studies an allele of bt on an inbred C57BL/6 background was used, as different genetic backgrounds can affect the expressivity of the bt phenotype [30],[31]. Since an Adamts20 mutation had not been specifically demonstrated in this particular bt allele, a complementation cross was performed between these bt mice and btBei1/+ mice. Seven out of 10 animals born exhibited a bt phenotype, consistent with the expected Mendelian ratios (50% bt) and indicative of a recessive allele of bt. This allele has now been designated bt9J and is listed at MGI.
###end p 13
###begin title 14
###xml 6 8 6 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 11 13 11 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 4 13 4 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 43 51 43 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 14 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The bt9J/bt9J mouse contains a mutation in Adamts20.
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 20 22 20 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 25 27 25 27 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 18 27 18 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 153 155 153 155 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 151 155 151 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 158 160 158 160 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 156 160 156 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 179 181 179 181 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 200 209 200 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wild-type</italic>

###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 4 12 4 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 39 41 39 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 44 46 44 46 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 295 297 295 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 293 297 293 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 338 346 338 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 387 393 387 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts</italic>
###xml 559 561 559 561 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 582 584 582 584 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 580 584 580 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 595 616 595 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 640 642 640 642 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 638 642 638 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 714 723 714 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 763 765 763 765 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 761 765 761 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 769 773 769 773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mri1</sup>
###xml 767 773 767 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Mri1</sup></italic>
###xml 779 781 779 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 836 838 836 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 298 302 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 322 327 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 332 337 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 394 399 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 585 589 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 672 677 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
The Adamts20 gene was sequenced from bt9J/bt9J genomic DNA in order to identify the molecular lesion. A single C to T point mutation was identified at nucleotide 2451, which is predicted to cause a missense mutation (Leu761Phe) in the spacer domain of ADAMTS20. The leucine residue mutated in bt9J mice is present in both mouse and human Adamts20 genes and is highly conserved among all Adamts mouse genes (present in 15 of the 19 genes). This suggests that Leu761 may be a critical residue for ADAMTS20 folding or for enzymatic function. We designed a TaqmanTM assay to genotype bt9J mice (see Materials and Methods). We determined that bt9J is the same strain as Mutant Mouse Resource Center (MMRC) strain #183 (Figure 1B). Although the missense mutations in bt9J, btMri1, and bt affect different domains of ADAMTS20, these and other bt alleles are recessive and exhibit very similar phenotypes, strongly suggesting they act as functional null alleles.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
###xml 74 76 74 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 79 81 79 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 72 81 72 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Initial Specification and Migration of Melanoblasts Is not Disrupted in bt9J/bt9J Embryos
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 144 152 144 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 221 223 221 223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 214 223 214 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 285 288 285 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
###xml 376 378 376 378 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 374 378 374 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 381 383 381 383 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 379 383 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 395 399 395 399 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mackenzie1">[18]</xref>
###xml 400 404 400 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hornyak1">[32]</xref>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 452 456 452 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 18 23 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 267 271 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
White spotting of mouse coats is typically caused by defective melanoblast development during embryogenesis. In order to elucidate when and how Adamts20 affects melanoblast development, melanoblast distribution in bt9J/bt9J embryos was examined. We generated C57BL/6 mice containing a Dct-LacZ transgene, which marks specified melanoblasts, and crossed these onto a C57BL/6 bt9J/bt9J background [18],[32]. Since there are no phenotypes associated with bt9J/+ adult animals, this heterozygous genotype served as a control for this study.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 54 56 54 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 59 62 59 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
###xml 74 76 74 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 72 76 72 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 79 81 79 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 82 86 82 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 123 132 123 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000003.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 137 145 137 145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 338 348 338 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000003.s001">Figures S1</xref>
###xml 353 369 353 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2A and 2C</xref>
###xml 424 426 424 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 422 426 422 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 429 431 429 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 454 464 454 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000003.s001">Figures S1</xref>
###xml 469 485 469 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2B and 2D</xref>
###xml 670 672 670 672 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 668 672 668 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 675 677 675 677 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 673 677 673 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 687 694 687 694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 705 721 705 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2A and 2C</xref>
###xml 833 835 833 835 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 831 835 831 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 838 840 838 840 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 836 840 836 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
We compared melanoblast distribution in whole mount bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos at E11.5 through E16.5 (Figure S1 and Figure 2). In E11.5 and E12.5 control embryos, melanoblasts had completed their initial migration from the neural tube and were distributed evenly across the dorsal and lateral surfaces of the embryo (Figures S1 and Figure 2A and 2C). A similar distribution pattern in E11.5 and E12.5 bt9J/bt9J embryos was observed (Figures S1 and Figure 2B and 2D). Quantification of melanoblasts in the head and the presumptive belt region of the trunk of E12.5 whole mount embryos showed no difference in melanoblast number between control and bt9J/bt9J embryos (Table 1, boxes in Figure 2A and 2C). These results show that initial specification and migration of NC-derived melanoblasts is not disrupted in bt9J/bt9J animals.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
###xml 71 73 71 73 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 76 78 76 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 69 78 69 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Melanoblast distribution is defective in whole mount E13.5 and older bt9J/bt9J embryos.
###end title 20

###xml 553 560 550 557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t001">Table 1</xref>

###begin title 22
Quantitation of melanoblasts in whole mount embryos.
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 232 240 232 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 262 283 262 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
Shown are the average number of melanoblasts quantitated, standard deviations, and the number of samples in parentheses. P values are included with ** indicating highly significant values. The regions quantitated are represented in Figure 2 and described in the Materials and Methods.

Melanoblast Distribution Is Reduced only in the Trunk of bt9J/bt9J Embryos

###xml 513 538 513 538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2F, 2H, 2J, and 2L</xref>

###xml 693 700 693 700 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 711 732 711 732 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2E, 2G, 2I, 2K</xref>
###xml 881 883 881 883 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###xml 886 890 886 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 904 920 904 920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2M and 2O</xref>
###xml 933 935 933 935 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 931 935 931 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>

###xml 941 945 941 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1067 1083 1067 1083 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2N and 2P</xref>
###xml 1168 1170 1168 1170 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1166 1170 1166 1170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1173 1177 1173 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1188 1190 1188 1190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1186 1190 1186 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1193 1195 1193 1195 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1191 1195 1191 1195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1196 1200 1196 1200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1214 1230 1214 1230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2O and 2P</xref>
###xml 1281 1283 1281 1283 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1279 1283 1279 1283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1286 1288 1286 1288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1284 1288 1284 1288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1289 1293 1289 1293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1437 1446 1437 1446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000003.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 1515 1517 1515 1517 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1513 1517 1513 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1520 1522 1520 1522 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1518 1522 1518 1522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Since there was no defect in younger embryos, melanoblast distribution in bt9J/+; Dct-LacZ and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ E13.5-E16.5 embryos was compared (Figure 2E-2P). In E13.5 and E14.5 bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ embryos, the melanoblast population had expanded throughout the embryo and melanoblasts were distributed uniformly across dorsal and lateral surfaces of the trunk (Figure 2E, 2G, 2I, and 2K). In contrast, melanoblast distribution was specifically reduced in the trunk of E13.5 and E14.5 bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos (Figure 2F, 2H, 2J, and 2L). Quantitation of the head and trunk region of E13.5 and E14.5 bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos confirmed that the melanoblast defect was limited to the trunk (Table 1, boxes in Figure 2E, 2G, 2I, 2K) (p = 0.0000002 at E13.5, p = 0.000096 at E14.5). By E15.5 and E16.5, melanoblasts were distributed evenly on both dorsal and ventral surfaces of bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ embryos (Figure 2M and 2O). However bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos displayed a notable absence of melanoblasts on both surfaces in the region corresponding to the future belt (Figure 2N and 2P). Melanoblast distribution in the head and tail regions was similar between E16.5 bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos (Figure 2O and 2P). Close examination of the belt region in E16.5 bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos showed no accumulation of melanoblasts at the edges of the belt, as might be expected if migration into this region were impaired (Figure S2). Collectively, these analyses of the melanoblast distribution in bt9J/bt9J animals reveal the following: the phenotype is first apparent at E13.5, melanoblasts are reduced only in the trunk region (the location of the presumptive belt), and dorso-lateral melanoblast migration is not impaired.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 55 57 55 57 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 60 62 60 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 53 62 53 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Melanoblasts Are Present in All Skin Compartments of bt9J/bt9J Embryos
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 181 189 181 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 189 193 189 193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 194 198 194 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Silver1">[15]</xref>
###xml 231 239 231 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 471 480 471 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 485 492 485 492 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 499 520 499 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 629 631 629 631 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 627 631 627 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 634 636 634 636 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 632 636 632 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 637 641 637 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 757 764 757 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 840 847 840 847 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 852 864 852 864 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2E&#8211;2H</xref>
###xml 954 956 954 956 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 952 956 952 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 959 961 959 961 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 957 961 957 961 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 962 966 962 966 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1015 1017 1015 1017 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1013 1017 1013 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1020 1024 1020 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 1058 1067 1058 1067 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 1170 1172 1170 1172 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1168 1172 1168 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1175 1177 1175 1177 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1173 1177 1173 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
The melanoblast defect is first observed at E13.5, coincident with the timing of melanoblast migration from the dermis into the epidermis, and with generalized dermal expression of Adamts20[12],[15]. Therefore we hypothesized that Adamts20 may be required for normal distribution of melanoblasts in dermal and epidermal compartments of the skin. To address this, melanoblasts were quantified in the dermis, epidermis, and dermal-epidermal border in E13.5 trunk sections (Figure 3A and Table 2) (see Materials and Methods). In control trunk sections (n = 178) we observed an average of 33.6 melanoblasts per section, whereas in bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ sections (n = 179) there was an average two-fold reduction in melanoblast number (15.9 per section, p<0.0001) (Table 2). This finding is consistent with the analyses of whole mount embryos (see Table 1 and Figure 2E-2H). However, the relative distribution of melanoblasts within each of the skin layers in bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos did not differ significantly from bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ control embryos (p = 0.056) (Figure 3B). These results show that while melanoblast number is significantly reduced in the lumbar region of bt9J/bt9J embryos, melanoblast migration from the dermis into the epidermis is unaffected.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 55 57 55 57 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 60 62 60 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 53 62 53 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Melanoblast distribution in the skin layers of E13.5 bt9J/bt9J embryos is normal.
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 309 311 305 307 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 307 313 303 309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 326 328 322 324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 331 333 327 329 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 324 333 320 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 521 523 517 519 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 519 525 515 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 532 534 528 530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 537 539 533 535 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 530 539 526 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
(A) A cartoon representation of an E13.5 whole mount embryo showing the region between the fore- and hind-limbs from which 16 microm trunk sections were analyzed. (B) Pie charts representing the melanoblast distribution in the dermis (blue), epidermis (red), and dermal/epidermal border (yellow) from E13.5 bt9J/+ (top) and bt9J/bt9J (bottom) sections with the total number of melanoblasts indicated in parentheses (n = 2 embryos, each genotype). There was no significant difference in melanoblast distribution between bt9J/+ and bt9J/bt9J embryos (p = 0.056).
###end p 29
###begin title 30
Quantitation of Melanoblasts in sections through the head and trunk at E13.5.
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 202 210 202 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 327 329 327 329 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 325 331 325 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 338 340 338 340 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 343 345 343 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 336 345 336 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
At least 3 embryos of each genotype were analyzed. For the head, only horizontal sections containing one or both eyes were included. For the trunk, horizontal sections corresponding to regions shown in Figure 3 were included. The standard deviations are included in parentheses. The results of statistical analyses comparing bt9J/+ and bt9J/bt9J are included (NS = not significant and ** = p<0.0001, which is highly significant).
###end p 31
###begin title 32
###xml 2 4 2 4 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 7 9 7 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
bt9J/bt9J Embryos Exhibit Normal Melanoblast Proliferation but Defective Melanoblast Survival
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 58 60 58 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 56 60 56 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 61 65 61 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 162 166 162 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mackenzie1">[18]</xref>
###xml 185 187 185 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 270 272 270 272 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 268 272 268 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 275 277 275 277 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 273 277 273 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 348 350 348 350 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 346 350 346 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 353 357 353 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 368 370 368 370 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 366 370 366 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 373 375 373 375 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 371 375 371 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 376 380 376 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 401 411 401 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g003">Figures 3A</xref>
###xml 416 417 416 417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g004">4</xref>
###xml 536 548 533 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g004">Figure 4A&#8211;4C</xref>
###xml 616 618 613 615 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 614 618 611 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 621 623 618 620 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 619 623 616 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 709 718 706 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g004">Figure 4G</xref>
###xml 768 770 765 767 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 766 770 763 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 773 775 770 772 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 771 775 768 772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
At E13.5, when the defect in melanoblast development in bt9J/bt9J embryos is first apparent, melanoblasts are undergoing dramatic increases in cell proliferation [18]. To assess if the bt phenotype is caused by reduced melanoblast proliferation in the trunk region of bt9J/bt9J embryos, the mitotic index of melanoblasts at E13.5 was examined in bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ trunk sections (Figures 3A and 4). Melanoblasts undergoing mitosis were identified by co-expression of beta-galactosidase and phospho-histoneH3 (PH3) (Figure 4A-4C). The average percentage of dividing melanoblasts in control and bt9J/bt9J sections was not significantly different (2.94% and 3.03% respectively, p = 0.9067) (Figure 4G), suggesting that the melanoblast reduction in bt9J/bt9J embryos is not a consequence of abnormal proliferation.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 66 68 66 68 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 64 68 64 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 71 73 71 73 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 149 153 149 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wakamatsu1">[33]</xref>
###xml 296 306 293 303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g003">Figures 3A</xref>
###xml 311 316 308 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g004">4D&#8211;4F</xref>
###xml 401 403 398 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 399 403 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 406 408 403 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 404 408 401 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 409 413 406 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 441 443 438 440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 439 443 436 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 444 445 441 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</italic>
###xml 446 450 443 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 499 508 496 505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g004">Figure 4H</xref>
###xml 510 517 507 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 775 777 772 774 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 773 777 770 774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 780 782 777 779 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 778 782 775 779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 823 825 820 822 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 821 825 818 822 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 828 830 825 827 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 826 830 823 827 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 881 883 878 880 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 879 883 876 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 886 888 883 885 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 884 888 881 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 954 962 951 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
The reduced number of melanoblasts in the trunk region of E13.5 bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos could also be due to a failure of melanoblasts to survive [33]. To examine this, the apoptotic index of melanoblasts was quantitated from cells co-expressing beta-galactosidase and cleaved-caspase3 (CC3) (Figures 3A and 4D-4F). The average percentage of apoptotic melanoblasts was significantly increased in bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ sections relative to bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ sections (compare 8.4% to 1.2%, p<0.00005) (Figure 4H, Table 2). Apoptotic melanoblasts were apparent in both dorsal and ventral skin in control and mutant embryos. In addition, no significant differences were seen in the distribution of apoptotic, CC3+melanoblasts in the three skin compartments, as follows: dermal (bt9J/bt9J = 77.8%; control = 82.4%), epidermal (bt9J/bt9J = 14.8%; control = 5.8%), and dermal/epidermal (bt9J/bt9J = 7.4%; control = 11.85%), (p = 0.6133). These results show that Adamts20 is required for melanoblast survival in all cell layers of the trunk at E13.5.
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 259 266 259 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 372 376 372 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Baxter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wilkie1">[37]</xref>
###xml 664 666 664 666 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 662 666 662 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 669 671 669 671 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 667 671 667 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 672 676 672 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 690 697 690 697 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 90 94 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Adamts20 is expressed along the length of the embryo, yet the spotting phenotype in adult mice is evident only in the lumbar region. Therefore we examined melanoblast number and melanoblast apoptosis in a region outside of where the belt occurs, in the head (Table 2). In normal embryos, the density of melanoblasts is not the same in all regions, as previously described [34]-[37]. As expected, quantitation of melanoblasts in control embryos demonstrated that there were over three-fold more total melanoblasts in the head region than in the trunk (compare 110 versus 33.6, p = 0.0001). There was no difference in melanoblast number in the head of control and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos (Table 2), similar to what was seen in whole mount analyses.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 130 137 130 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000003-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 247 249 247 249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 245 249 245 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 250 254 250 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 397 405 397 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
The apoptotic index of melanoblasts varied in different regions of control embryos as well as between control and mutant embryos (Table 2). In control embryos, melanoblast apoptosis was lower in the head than in the trunk. Comparing control and bt9J/bt9J embryos, we found that apoptosis was increased in the head although to a lesser extent than observed in the trunk. This result indicates that Adamts20 is required for melanoblast survival throughout the embryo even though it does not result in white spotting in the head.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 18 20 18 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 16 20 16 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 23 25 23 25 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 21 25 21 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J Skin Fail To Respond to sKitl
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 54 58 54 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Steel1">[20]</xref>
###xml 59 63 59 63 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Ito1">[38]</xref>
###xml 164 172 164 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 178 182 178 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-WehrleHaller1">[21]</xref>
###xml 184 188 184 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Matsui1">[24]</xref>
###xml 189 193 189 193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida2">[26]</xref>
###xml 216 224 216 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 382 384 382 384 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 380 384 380 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 387 389 387 389 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 385 389 385 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 434 437 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 454 458 454 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 476 482 476 482 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 473 482 473 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 517 520 517 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 557 561 557 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Bernex1">[39]</xref>
###xml 562 566 562 566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hou1">[41]</xref>
###xml 583 591 583 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 595 597 595 597 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
