###xml 1288 1304 1288 1304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g005">Figure 5C and 5D</xref>
###xml 1306 1310 1306 1310 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Brannan1">[42]</xref>
###xml 1311 1315 1311 1315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Flanagan1">[43]</xref>
###xml 1332 1334 1332 1334 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1330 1334 1330 1334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1337 1339 1337 1339 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1335 1339 1335 1339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1368 1372 1368 1372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mitf</italic>
###xml 1376 1378 1376 1378 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1374 1378 1374 1378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1381 1383 1381 1383 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1388 1390 1388 1390 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mi</sup>
###xml 1379 1392 1379 1392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>;Mitf<sup>Mi</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 1443 1452 1443 1452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g005">Figure 5E</xref>
###xml 1490 1493 1490 1493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 1522 1524 1522 1524 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1520 1524 1520 1524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1527 1529 1527 1529 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1525 1529 1525 1529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 485 489 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 615 619 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 701 705 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 721 725 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1030 1034 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1340 1344 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Melanoblast survival is dependent upon Kit activation [20],[38] by Kit ligand (Kitl), which is expressed in the dermis in a similar temporal and spatial pattern to Adamts20[12], [21], [24]-[26]. We hypothesized that Adamts20 regulates melanoblast survival through modulation of Kit signaling, and assessed the effects of altered Kit signaling upon the extent of white spotting in bt9J/bt9J animals harboring various mutant alleles of Kit (MGI: 96677) or Kitl (MGI: 96974). Kittm1Alf/+ mice contain a null mutation in Kit and have primarily ventral spotting [39]-[41]. As depicted in Figure 5, bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ mice exhibited dramatically wider dorsal and ventral belts in comparison to bt9J/bt9J mice or Kittm1Alf/+ mice alone (Figure 5A and 5B). The increased spotting was a synergistic effect rather than an additive one (compare 46.9% of dorsal and ventral surfaces in bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ with 11.2% and 9.1% in Kittm1Alf/+ and bt9J/bt9J, respectively). Synergistic increases in spotting were also observed in bt9J/bt9J mice carrying mutant alleles of Kitl. Heterozygosity for either KitlSl, a null allele, or KitlSl-d, a deletion that generates short soluble Kitl but not membrane-bound Kitl, combined with homozygosity for bt9J resulted in synergistically increased spotting (Figure 5C and 5D) [42],[43]. In contrast, bt9J/bt9J mice carrying a mutation in Mitf (bt9J/bt9J;MitfMi/+) (MGI: 104554) exhibited no synergistic spotting (Figure 5E). These results show that decreasing Kit signaling exacerbates the bt9J/bt9J phenotype.
###end p 38

###xml 56 58 56 58 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###xml 89 91 85 87 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###xml 699 701 695 697 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 697 703 693 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 717 719 713 715 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 722 724 718 720 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

(A-F) Representative immunofluorescence images depicting 16 microm trunk sections from bt9J/bt9J E13.5 embryos assayed for proliferation (A-C) and apoptosis (D-F). Proliferating melanoblasts were identified by staining sections for LacZ (cytoplasmic red, A) and PH3 (nuclear green, B), and their co-localization together with nuclear DAPI staining (blue, C). Apoptotic melanoblasts were identified by staining sections for LacZ (cytoplasmic red, D) and CC3 (cytoplasmic green, E), and their co-localization together with DAPI (blue, F). (G-H) The Y axis (%Dct+PH3+ and %Dct+CC3) indicates the average percentage of total melanoblasts per section that are PH3 positive (G) or CC3 positive (H), for bt9J/+ (blue) and bt9J/bt9J (red) E13.5 embryos (n = 5 embryos for each genotype). The total number of sections and melanoblasts analyzed are listed beneath each graph, as well as the standard deviations. Asterisks indicate highly significant P values. The scale bars are: (A-F) 0.5 microM.

###begin p 43
###xml 16 19 16 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W-v</sup>
###xml 13 19 13 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>W-v</sup></italic>
###xml 75 79 75 79 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mackenzie1">[18]</xref>
###xml 151 153 151 153 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 149 153 149 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 156 158 156 158 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 154 158 154 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 206 208 206 208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 204 208 204 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 211 213 211 213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 209 213 209 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 296 298 296 298 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 294 298 294 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 301 303 301 303 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 299 303 299 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 331 333 331 333 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 329 333 329 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 334 335 334 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</italic>
###xml 339 345 339 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 336 345 336 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 354 356 354 356 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 352 356 352 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 359 361 359 361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 357 361 357 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 365 371 365 371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 362 371 362 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 383 392 383 392 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000003.s003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 408 414 408 414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 405 414 405 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 429 433 429 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LacZ</italic>
###xml 450 453 450 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 560 563 557 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 608 610 605 607 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 606 610 603 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 611 612 608 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</italic>
###xml 616 622 613 619 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 613 622 610 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 631 633 628 630 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 629 633 626 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 636 638 633 635 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 634 638 631 635 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 642 648 639 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 639 648 636 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 784 786 781 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
Heterozygous KitW-v mutations reduce melanoblast number beginning at E10.5 [18], which is three days prior to the onset of the melanoblast defect in bt9J/bt9J. To determine if decreasing Kit signaling in bt9J/bt9J embryos would lead to an earlier defect in melanoblast development than seen in bt9J/bt9J alone, we examined E12.5 bt9J/+;Kittm1Alf/+ and bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ embryos (Figure S3). Since the Kittm1Alf mutation is a LacZ knock-in at the Kit locus, we monitored melanoblasts using beta-galactosidase staining. There was no detectable difference in Kit-positive melanoblast distribution between bt9J/+;Kittm1Alf/+ and bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ embryos at E12.5. These results demonstrate that the synergistic defect in melanoblast development does not precede the onset of the bt phenotype at E13.5.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 84 92 84 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 138 140 138 140 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 136 140 136 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 143 145 143 145 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###xml 188 195 188 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ex vivo</italic>
###xml 268 272 268 272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Jordan1">[44]</xref>
###xml 273 277 273 277 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Kashiwagi2">[46]</xref>
###xml 296 298 296 298 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###xml 316 318 316 318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 314 318 314 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 321 323 321 323 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 319 323 319 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 324 328 324 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 383 390 383 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ex vivo</italic>
###xml 482 484 482 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 493 501 493 501 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 616 625 616 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 703 705 703 705 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 701 705 701 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 708 710 708 710 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 706 710 706 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 711 715 711 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 798 807 798 807 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 858 860 858 860 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 856 860 856 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 863 865 863 865 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 861 865 861 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 866 870 866 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 884 900 884 900 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g002">Figure 2O and 2P</xref>
The synergistic interaction studies indicate that Kit signaling may be disrupted in Adamts20 mutant animals. To test if melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J embryos could respond to sKitl we used an ex vivo embryonic skin explant assay using dorsal trunk skin from E13.5 embryos [44]-[46]. Observation of bt9J/+;Dct-LacZ and bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ skin after four days in culture demonstrated that ex vivo explant culture conditions could recapitulate both normal melanoblast colonization and the bt defect (Figure 6). Melanoblasts in the control skin entered hair follicles and were distributed evenly across the explant (n = 5) (Figure 6A). While some melanoblasts survived and migrated into hair follicles in the bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ skin, in a large domain of the explant the melanoblasts were reduced (n = 5) (Figure 6B), similar to the phenotype of whole mount E16.5 bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ embryos (Figure 2O and 2P).
###end p 44
###begin title 45
###xml 18 20 18 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 23 25 23 25 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 16 25 16 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J skin do not respond to soluble Kitl.
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 76 78 73 75 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 74 84 71 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+;Dct</italic>
###xml 101 103 98 100 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>

###begin p 47
###xml 105 109 105 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Jordan1">[44]</xref>
###xml 170 174 170 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Ito1">[38]</xref>
###xml 355 357 355 357 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 353 357 353 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 360 362 360 362 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 358 362 358 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 407 409 407 409 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 405 409 405 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 412 414 412 414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 410 414 410 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 481 483 481 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 673 682 673 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g006">Figure 6C</xref>
###xml 719 721 719 721 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 717 721 717 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 724 726 724 726 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 722 726 722 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 727 731 727 731 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 812 821 812 821 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 1021 1030 1021 1030 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20,</italic>
###xml 1124 1126 1124 1126 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1122 1126 1122 1126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1129 1131 1129 1131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1127 1131 1127 1131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1187 1189 1187 1189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 1246 1248 1246 1248 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1251 1253 1251 1253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1244 1253 1244 1253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Previous studies showed that melanoblasts within embryonic skin cultures respond to soluble Kitl (sKitl) [44] and that sKitl promotes melanoblast survival in NC cultures [38]. ADAMTS20 could be required for proteolytic cleavage of Kit or Kitl, or for modifying additional molecules necessary for Kit signaling. To test if Kit signaling was defective in bt9J/bt9J embryos, we asked whether melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J embryos could respond to sKitl and whether sKitl could rescue the bt phenotype. Similar to studies by Jordan et. al, an increase in melanoblast number and colonization of hair follicles was observed in control skin exposed to sKitl as compared to FBS alone (Figure 6C, n = 5). In contrast, exposure of bt9J/bt9J;Dct-LacZ skin (n = 7) to sKitl did not restore melanoblasts to the presumptive belt (Figure 6D). Interestingly, melanoblasts at the rostral and caudal regions of the trunk did not increase in number, even though these are outside of the expected belt. These results show that in the absence of Adamts20, melanoblasts are unable to respond to sKitl, indicating that Kit signaling is disrupted in bt9J/bt9J mutants. Furthermore, since sKitl could not rescue the bt phenotype, it suggests that the melanoblast defect in bt9J/bt9J animals is not caused by defective cleavage of Kitl.
###end p 47
###begin title 48
###xml 26 34 26 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 74 81 74 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
ADAMTS20 Cleaves Versican in vitro and Is Necessary for Versican Cleavage in vivo
###end title 48
###begin p 49
###xml 33 41 33 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 360 363 360 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Apte1">[1]</xref>
###xml 364 367 364 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Porter1">[2]</xref>
###xml 368 372 368 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 563 567 563 567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Dutt1">[48]</xref>
###xml 568 572 568 572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Perris1">[52]</xref>
We explored the possibility that Adamts20 could regulate melanoblast survival through additional pathways. One of the best-understood activities of ADAMTS proteases is processing of various ECM substrates. Of note, ADAMTS20 is most closely related phylogenetically to ADAMTS metalloproteases that specifically process chondroitin sulfate proteoglycans (CSPGs) [1],[2],[47]. Although no substrates for ADAMTS20 have been identified, the CSPG versican is enriched in the skin and implicated in NC development, making it an excellent candidate substrate of ADAMTS20 [48]-[52].
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 12 20 12 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican</italic>
###xml 25 33 25 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 60 67 60 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 174 182 174 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican</italic>
###xml 187 195 187 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 517 524 517 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
We examined Versican and Adamts20 expression by whole mount in situ hybridization in wild-type embryos. At E12.5, when melanoblasts are widely distributed in the trunk, both Versican and Adamts20 are expressed broadly across the trunk, overlapping in many regions of the skin and the developing mammary ducts (data not shown). Since both versican and ADAMTS20 are secreted proteins, the expression patterns of their RNAs relative to each other and to melanoblasts support the possibility of a functional relationship in vivo.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 148 157 148 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 160 168 160 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican</italic>
###xml 226 236 226 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">VersicanV1</italic>
###xml 278 282 278 282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Carrino1">[53]</xref>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zimmermann1">[56]</xref>
###xml 446 450 446 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Sandy1">[57]</xref>
###xml 615 623 615 623 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 625 634 625 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 734 741 734 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 795 799 795 799 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 825 834 825 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro,</italic>
We assessed the ability of ADAMTS20 to process versican by expressing ADAMTS20 in 293 cells, and subsequently incubating these cells with versican (Figure 7A). Versican is alternatively spliced to generate four isoforms, with VersicanV1 being the dominant variant in adult skin [53]-[56]. Versican cleavage was examined using anti-DPEAEE antibody, which specifically recognizes the neo-epitope generated by ADAMTS cleavage of versicanV1 (70 KDa) [57]. While secreted media from 293 cells alone exhibited little to no cleavage of versican, versican processing was evident in secreted media from 293 cells expressing Adamts20 (Figure 7A). As a positive control, cleaved versican was also evident in secreted media from cells expressing Adamts9, which has previously been shown to process versican [47]. These results show that in vitro, versican is a substrate for cleavage by ADAMTS20.
###end p 51
###begin title 52
###xml 26 34 26 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 39 46 39 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
ADAMTS20 cleaves versican in vitro and in vivo.
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 168 176 168 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 197 205 197 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9,</italic>
###xml 299 301 299 301 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 297 303 297 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 310 312 310 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 315 317 315 317 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 308 317 308 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 462 465 455 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</italic>
###xml 482 484 475 477 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 487 489 480 482 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 480 489 473 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 847 849 833 835 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 852 854 838 840 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 845 854 831 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
(A,B) Western analyses probed with anti-DPEAEE that recognizes the 70 KDa versican cleavage product. (A) Protein extracts from 293 cells transfected with vector alone, Adamts20 (2 experiments) and Adamts9, and incubated with versican. (B) Protein extracts of E15.5 day old skin from six different bt9J/+ and bt9J/bt9J embryos. Anti-alpha-Tubulin serves as a loading control and anti-GAG betaindicates levels of total versican. (C-J) Immunofluorescence images of +/+ (C,E,G, I) or bt9J/bt9J (D,F,H,J) E15.5 10 microm trunk (C-H) and forelimb (I,J) sections stained with anti-DPEAAE (C,D,I,J), anti-DPEAAE and DPEAEE peptide (E,F), and anti-GAG beta (G,H). The anti-DPEAEE staining in the proliferating layer of the epidermis (indicated by arrows) is reduced dramatically in trunk sections and reduced to a lesser extent in forelimb sections from bt9J/bt9J embryos. The scale bars are: (C-F,I,J) 50 microM, (G,H) 100 microM.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 59 61 59 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 57 61 57 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 62 63 62 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</italic>
###xml 70 72 70 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 68 72 68 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 142 149 142 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 151 160 151 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 219 221 219 221 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 217 221 217 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 224 226 224 226 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 566 575 560 569 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 642 650 636 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 705 712 699 706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Analysis of skin extracts from the dorsal trunk of E15.5 bt9J/+ and bt9J/bt9J embryos showed ADAMTS20 is also necessary for versican cleavage in vivo (Figure 7B). The levels of the cleaved 70 KDa band were reduced in bt9J/bt9J extracts compared to control extracts (n =  4 experiments). We also observed a reduction in levels of a 220 KDa band corresponding to the V0 isoform (data not shown). In contrast, there was no alteration in total versican, which was assessed using a GAG beta antibody that recognizes the GAG beta domains of full-length versicanV0 and V1 (Figure 7B). Collectively, these results show that ADAMTS20 cleaves versican in vitro and that it is required for versican cleavage in skin in vivo.
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 174 177 174 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</italic>
###xml 185 187 185 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 190 192 190 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 188 192 188 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 202 214 202 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7C&#8211;7H</xref>
###xml 220 223 220 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</italic>
###xml 365 374 365 374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 504 508 504 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zimmermann1">[56]</xref>
###xml 525 528 525 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</italic>
###xml 541 543 541 543 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 539 543 539 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 546 548 546 548 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 544 548 544 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 627 636 627 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
###xml 760 776 760 776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7E and 7F</xref>
###xml 825 828 825 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</italic>
###xml 844 846 844 846 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 842 846 842 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 849 851 849 851 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 847 851 847 851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 978 994 978 994 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7G and 7H</xref>
###xml 1091 1093 1091 1093 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1089 1093 1089 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1096 1098 1096 1098 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1094 1098 1094 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1193 1209 1193 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g007">Figure 7I and 7J</xref>
###xml 1250 1252 1250 1252 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1248 1252 1248 1252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1255 1257 1255 1257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1253 1257 1253 1257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 493 498 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Immunofluorescence was performed to evaluate the spatial pattern of versican cleavage in embryonic skin. Versican expression was assessed on trunk sections of E15.5 C57BL/6 (+/+) and bt9J/bt9J embryos (Figure 7C-7H). In +/+ sections, cleaved versican was evident in the dermal mesenchyme and was enriched in the proliferating basal layer of the epidermis (arrow in Figure 7C) but was excluded from the outermost layer of the epidermis, in a similar pattern to that of intact versican in adult human skin [56]. In contrast to +/+ sections, bt9J/bt9J sections displayed a dramatic reduction in cleaved versican in the epidermis (Figure 7D). Inclusion of the DPEAEE peptide in the staining procedure demonstrated the specificity of the antibody for this peptide (Figure 7E and 7F). Total versican expression was similar in both +/+ sections and bt9J/bt9J sections, with high expression in the basement membrane, dermis, and dermal condensations, but lower levels in the epidermis (Figure 7G and 7H). Outside of the belt region, at the level of the forelimb, the levels of cleaved versican in bt9J/bt9J sections were reduced relative to wild-type, but not to the same extent as seen in the trunk (Figure 7I and 7J). Together these results show that in bt9J/bt9J embryos, levels of processed versican, but not total versican, are reduced in the skin of the embryonic trunk, and show that ADAMTS20 is necessary for versican remodeling during melanoblast development.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 12 20 12 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Adamts9 and Adamts20 Act Cooperatively To Regulate Melanoblast Development
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 9 17 9 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>

###xml 110 112 110 112 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 108 112 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 115 117 115 117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 113 117 113 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 446 454 446 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 465 472 465 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts5</italic>
###xml 493 501 493 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9,</italic>
###xml 673 677 673 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 678 682 678 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Jungers1">[58]</xref>
###xml 683 687 683 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Reymond1">[59]</xref>
###xml 806 814 806 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 877 885 877 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 913 915 913 915 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 897 915 897 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9 (Adamts9<sup>ko</sup></italic>
###xml 936 938 936 938 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 920 939 920 939 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts5 (Adamts5<sup>ko</sup>)</italic>
Although Adamts20 is expressed across the length of the embryo [12], only the lumbar region of the trunk in bt9J/bt9J mutants shows dramatic reduction of melanoblasts and white spotting. Given that ADAMTS20 belongs to a large family of closely related metalloproteases, we reasoned that partial redundancy with other metalloproteases might account for the higher proportion of melanoblasts surviving outside of the lumbar region. The two closest Adamts20 homologs, Adamts5 (GeneID: 23794) and Adamts9, are both expressed in the embryonic skin along the length of the embryo and are both versicanases, making them excellent candidates for regulating melanoblast development [47],[58],[59](Bon-Hun Koo and S.S. Apte, unpublished data). To test if these metalloprotease genes were functionally redundant with Adamts20, we evaluated the extent of white spotting in mutants lacking Adamts20 and either Adamts9 (Adamts9ko) or Adamts5 (Adamts5ko).
###end p 57

###xml 1593 1602 1593 1602 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g008">Figure 8F</xref>
###xml 1650 1654 1650 1654 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>
###xml 1657 1661 1657 1661 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>

###xml 1648 1681 1648 1681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Bei1</sup>/bt<sup>Bei1</sup>;Adamts5<sup>ko</sup>/Adamts5<sup>ko</sup></italic>
###xml 1712 1716 1712 1716 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>
###xml 1719 1723 1719 1723 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bei1</sup>
###xml 1710 1723 1710 1723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>Bei1</sup>/bt<sup>Bei1</sup></italic>
###xml 1756 1763 1756 1763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts5</italic>
###xml 1790 1792 1790 1792 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1788 1792 1788 1792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1795 1797 1795 1797 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1793 1797 1793 1797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 1824 1840 1824 1840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9, Adamts5</italic>
###xml 195 199 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1682 1686 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Adamts9ko homozygotes are lethal prior to gastrulation (H. Enomoto and S. Apte, submitted) therefore we used Adamts9ko heterozygotes to examine a functional overlap between Adamts9 and 20. While mice heterozygous for mutation of Adamts20 and 9 are viable, bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ animals die shortly after birth (H. Enomoto and S. Apte, submitted). We examined pigmentation in newborn animals that were wild-type, bt9J/+;Adamts9ko/+, bt9J/bt9J, or bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+. Skin pelts containing dorsal and ventral surfaces and spanning the entire trunk region were removed from newborn pups (Figure 8A). Although not externally obvious until 4-5 days after birth, melanoblasts can be seen as clusters of pigmented cells on the dermal side of the P0 epidermis. In all skin samples, pigmentation was apparent primarily on dorsal surfaces as shown by schematic representations in Figure 8B-8E. In the skin from +/+ and bt9J/+;Adamts9ko/+ animals, pigmentation was distributed uniformly between anterior and posterior boundaries of the skin samples (n = 4 each) (Figures 8B and 8C). In the bt9J/bt9J skin samples (n = 6), a partial de-pigmentation was observed on about 50% of the anterior-posterior length, consistent with the likely boundaries of "belted" and "non-belted" regions (Figure 8D). However, in the bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ skin samples (n = 5), de-pigmentation was apparent on 75% of the anterior-posterior length (Figure 8E). Our analyses showed a statistically significant increase in the severity of de-pigmentation in bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ skin compared to that seen in bt9J/bt9J skin (Figure 8F). In contrast, the pigmentation phenotype in btBei1/btBei1;Adamts5ko/Adamts5ko mice was similar to that of btBei1/btBei1 animals indicating that loss of Adamts5 does not exacerbate the bt9J/bt9J phenotype and that unlike Adamts9, Adamts5 does not participate in melanoblast development (D. McCullough and S. Apte, unpublished data).
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 12 20 12 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Adamts9 and Adamts20 act redundantly to regulate pigmentation.
###end title 59
