###begin p 61
###xml 48 50 48 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 60 62 60 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 51 64 51 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+;Adamts9<sup>ko</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 70 72 70 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 68 72 68 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 85 87 85 87 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 73 89 73 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>;Adamts9<sup>ko</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 130 137 130 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 157 163 157 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pmel17</italic>
###xml 338 340 338 340 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 336 340 336 340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 343 345 343 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 353 355 353 355 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 341 357 341 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>;Adamts9<sup>ko</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 380 382 380 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 378 382 378 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 392 394 392 394 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 383 396 383 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+;Adamts9<sup>ko</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 524 540 524 540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000003-g008">Figure 8G and 8H</xref>
###xml 571 578 571 578 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 583 591 583 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 90 94 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
In order to assess melanoblast development in bt9J/+;Adamts9ko/+and bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ mice, E13.5 embryos were examined using in situ hybridization with Pmel17 (GeneID: 20431), a marker specific for melanoblasts. Similar to what was observed in newborn skin, there was a significant reduction in melanoblasts in the trunk region of bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ embryos compared to bt9J/+;Adamts9ko/+ embryos (data not shown). Importantly, there was also a significant reduction of melanoblasts in regions outside of the trunk (Figure 8G and 8H). These results indicate that Adamts9 and Adamts20 are partially redundant during melanoblast development not only in the trunk but in the head as well.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
Discussion
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 183 192 183 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20,</italic>
###xml 347 355 347 355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 393 402 393 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C.elegans</italic>
###xml 412 417 412 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gon-1</italic>
###xml 444 452 444 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 485 489 485 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 491 495 491 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Blelloch1">[27]</xref>
###xml 496 500 496 500 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hesselson1">[29]</xref>
###xml 619 627 619 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 12 17 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 116 121 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 393 402 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C.elegans</span>
Analysis of mouse coat color mutants has yielded mechanistic insights into normal developmental pathways as well as human disease processes. In this paper we explored how mutation of Adamts20, a secreted metalloprotease that is not expressed in melanoblasts, can disrupt melanoblast development and cause white spotting. The expression pattern of Adamts20, along with studies performed on the C.elegans ortholog Gon-1, initially suggested that Adamts20 regulated melanoblast migration [12], [27]-[29]. However, rather than this predicted requirement for melanoblast migration, we have identified an unexpected role for Adamts20 in melanoblast survival. Our results have implications not only for understanding mechanisms of melanoblast development and pigmentation-associated diseases but also for the biological functions of secreted metalloproteases.
###end p 63
###begin title 64
###xml 12 20 12 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Mutation of Adamts20 Increases Melanoblast Apoptosis
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 43 45 43 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 48 50 48 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 41 50 41 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 251 254 251 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 321 323 321 323 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 314 323 314 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 402 405 402 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 407 411 407 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mitf</italic>
###xml 413 417 413 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pax3</italic>
###xml 432 437 432 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ednrb</italic>
###xml 457 462 457 462 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sox10</italic>
###xml 546 550 546 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Silver1">[15]</xref>
The most striking alteration observed in bt9J/bt9J embryos was a reduction in trunk melanoblasts beginning at E13.5. Early events of melanoblast specification, migration, proliferation and survival were not affected, as the number and distribution of Dct-LacZ-positive melanoblasts was similar between control and bt9J/bt9J embryos up to E12.5. This result contrasts many melanoblast mutants including Kit, Mitf, Pax3 (MGI: 97487), Ednrb (MGI: 102720), and Sox10 (MGI: 98358), in which melanoblast defects can be observed as early as E10.5-E11.5 [15].
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 108 110 108 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 113 115 113 115 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 106 115 106 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 125 128 125 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
###xml 648 652 648 652 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wilkie1">[37]</xref>
###xml 653 657 653 657 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Jordan2">[60]</xref>
###xml 869 877 869 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Multiple lines of evidence also indicate that later stages of melanoblast migration were not defective in bt9J/bt9J embryos. Dct-LacZ-positive cells did not accumulate dorsally or in the dermis, suggesting that melanoblast migration along the dorso-lateral pathway and between skin layers was normal. It is also unlikely that melanoblasts undergo cell death as a result of or subsequent to failed migration, as apoptotic melanoblasts were apparent in both dorsal and ventral regions of mutant embryos and in similar proportions within dermal and epidermal compartments. Our results also exclude a defect in the second wave of melanoblast migration [37],[60], since melanoblasts did not accumulate at the belt edges in E16.5 embryos. Instead, our results show that reduction of melanoblasts is due to the seven-fold increase in apoptosis observed in the trunk region of Adamts20 mutant embryos.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
###xml 20 28 20 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Why Do Mutations in Adamts20 Cause a Belt?
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 41 49 41 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
We propose that the white belt occurs in Adamts20 mutants for a combination of three factors: uneven densities of melanoblasts along the length of normal embryos, regional differences in apoptosis, and functional redundancy with other metalloproteases.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 147 151 147 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Cable1">[17]</xref>
###xml 153 157 153 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Baxter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 158 160 158 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wilkie1">37</xref>
###xml 470 478 470 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 580 582 580 582 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 585 587 585 587 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 578 587 578 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 593 596 593 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
In wild-type animals there are fewer embryonic melanoblasts in the trunk relative to other areas of the body, as shown in this study and by others [17], [34]-37. Related to this, many of the coat color mutants exhibit spotting in the lumbar level of the trunk suggesting that melanoblasts in this region are particularly sensitive to genetic perturbation, perhaps due to reduced numbers. This suggests that if melanoblast numbers were further reduced along the trunk in Adamts20 mutants, the resulting belt would be wider. Indeed this was the case since genetic interactions of bt9J/bt9J with Kit mutations caused a wider belt as opposed to increased spotting in the head.
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 8 16 8 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 119 127 119 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 170 172 170 172 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 163 172 163 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 485 487 485 487 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 490 492 490 492 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 483 492 483 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Second, Adamts20 is required for melanoblast survival throughout the embryo, consistent with the expression pattern of Adamts20 along the length of the embryo. In bt9J/bt9J embryos, we found significant increases in apoptosis in both head and trunk regions. Importantly, the proportion of melanoblasts undergoing apoptosis was much more pronounced in the trunk than in the head. Thus a combination of increased apoptosis and lower initial melanoblast number in the trunk region of a bt9J/bt9J mutant depletes melanoblast numbers to levels at which it cannot generate adequate pigmentation.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 7 15 7 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 127 135 127 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9.</italic>
###xml 143 145 143 145 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 148 150 148 150 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 141 150 141 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 188 195 188 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 283 285 283 285 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 288 290 288 290 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 281 290 281 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 297 304 297 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 324 332 324 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 435 442 435 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 442 444 442 444 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 445 452 445 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 452 454 452 454 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 528 535 528 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 591 598 591 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 675 677 675 677 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 673 677 673 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 680 682 680 682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 690 692 690 692 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 678 694 678 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>;Adamts9<sup>ko</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 846 853 846 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 291 295 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 455 459 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Third, Adamts20 mutant animals have limited white spotting due to functional redundancy with other metalloproteases, including Adamts9. In a bt9J/bt9J background, loss of a single copy of Adamts9 results in reduced melanoblast numbers in the trunk as well as in the head. Thus, in bt9J/bt9J mice, Adamts9 can compensate for Adamts20 deficiency in regions of higher melanoblast number such as the head. The early embryonic lethality of Adamts9ko/Adamts9ko mice makes it impossible to currently assess the absolute requirement of Adamts9 in pigmentation. However, the widespread expression of Adamts9 in the skin paired with the dramatic defect in melanoblast development in bt9J/bt9J;Adamts9ko/+ animals predict an even greater pigmentation defect in a homozygous background. These future analyses will depend upon the generation of a conditional Adamts9 knock-out in the skin.
###end p 71
###begin title 72
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Adamts20 Modulates Kit Signaling
###end title 72
###begin p 73
###xml 25 33 25 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 107 110 107 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 137 139 137 139 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 142 144 142 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 140 144 140 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 148 154 148 154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 145 154 145 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 155 156 155 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</italic>
###xml 217 219 217 219 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 222 224 222 224 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 215 224 215 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 324 327 324 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 404 412 404 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 414 417 414 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 422 426 422 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 441 445 441 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 447 451 447 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Cable1">[17]</xref>
###xml 453 457 453 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Steel1">[20]</xref>
###xml 459 463 459 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Matsui1">[24]</xref>
###xml 464 468 464 468 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida2">[26]</xref>
###xml 469 473 469 473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Keshet1">[61]</xref>
Our results suggest that Adamts20 is required for melanoblast survival at least in part through modulating Kit signaling. We show that bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ mutants exhibit synergistic spotting, and melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J skin cultures are unable to respond to sKitl. This mechanism is consistent with the requirement of Kit signaling for melanoblast survival as well as the overlapping expression of Adamts20, Kit and Kitl in the dermis [12], [17], [20], [24]-[26],[61].
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 178 186 178 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 214 217 214 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 375 377 375 377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 380 382 380 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 373 382 373 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 467 472 467 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit/+</italic>
###xml 481 485 481 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Cable1">[17]</xref>
###xml 486 490 486 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mackenzie1">[18]</xref>
###xml 505 508 505 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 597 599 597 599 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 602 604 602 604 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 595 604 595 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 638 646 638 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 689 697 689 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 752 754 752 754 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 755 759 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Kit signaling is essential for several events in melanoblast development beginning at E10.5 and including both migration and survival. Yet our findings indicate that mutation of Adamts20 modulates only a subset of Kit functions, namely survival, and only during a defined window of time, around E13.5, rather than throughout development. This is evidenced by the fact that bt9J/bt9J embryos do not show altered melanoblast development prior to E13.5, such as seen in Kit/+ embryos [17],[18]. In addition, Kit heterozygous mutations do not exacerbate the onset of the melanoblast defect in E12.5 bt9J/bt9J embryos, as would be expected if Adamts20 were required earlier. The stage at which Adamts20 disrupts melanoblast development may also explain why bt mice do not exhibit extensive ventral spotting like other white spotted mutants that impede earlier events in development.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 70 73 70 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 134 136 134 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 139 141 139 141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 132 141 132 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 205 207 205 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 207 211 207 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida1">[23]</xref>
###xml 212 216 212 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Yoshida3">[62]</xref>
###xml 164 168 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 227 231 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 312 316 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 471 475 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Given these observations, it is notable that restricted disruption of Kit, during the embryonic period associated with onset of the bt9J/bt9J phenotype, results in mice with spotting phenotypes similar to bt[23],[62]. Pregnant mice injected with neutralizing Kit antibodies between E10.5 and E13.0 give birth to mice exhibiting white belts. In contrast, injection of these Kit antibodies into pregnant animals prior to E10.5 and after E13.0 results in mostly unpigmented mice.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 40 44 40 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W-sh</sup>
###xml 51 56 51 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W-57J</sup>
###xml 60 65 60 65 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W-57J</sup>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W-bd</sup>
###xml 37 80 37 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>W-sh</sup>/+, Kit<sup>W-57J</sup>/Kit<sup>W-57J</sup>, and Kit<sup>W-bd</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 153 156 153 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Duttlinger1">[35]</xref>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Duttlinger2">[63]</xref>
###xml 187 191 187 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Kluppel1">[64]</xref>
###xml 261 267 261 267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Ber</sup>
###xml 258 267 258 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm1Ber</sup></italic>
###xml 275 281 275 281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm2Ber</sup>
###xml 272 281 272 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>tm2Ber</sup></italic>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Kimura1">[65]</xref>
###xml 546 552 546 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">belted</italic>
###xml 581 589 581 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 671 678 671 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 81 85 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 282 286 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 553 557 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
A white belt/band is also evident in KitW-sh/+, KitW-57J/KitW-57J, and KitW-bd/+ mice that carry mutations in Kit regulatory sequences and cause altered Kit expression patterns [35],[63],[64]. In addition, Kimura and colleagues describe belted phenotypes in Kittm1Ber and Kittm2Ber mice containing targeted mutations of Kit at tyrosine residues 567 and 569, amino acids essential for proper phosphorylation and downstream signaling [65]. It is interesting that disruption of these specific amino acids results in spotting similar to that seen in belted mice, and we speculate that Adamts20 may be required for efficient Kit phosphorylation at these sites in melanoblasts in vivo.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 250 258 250 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 326 330 326 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Chesneau1">[66]</xref>
###xml 331 335 331 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zou1">[69]</xref>
###xml 395 397 395 397 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 400 402 400 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 393 402 393 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 516 518 516 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 570 572 570 572 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 575 577 575 577 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 568 577 568 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 629 633 629 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 659 663 659 663 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sl-d</sup>
###xml 655 665 655 665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KitL<sup>Sl-d</sup>/+</italic>
###xml 703 707 703 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Brannan1">[42]</xref>
###xml 708 712 708 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Flanagan1">[43]</xref>
###xml 713 717 713 717 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Tajima1">[70]</xref>
###xml 788 792 788 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 861 864 861 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit</italic>
###xml 914 916 914 916 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 919 921 919 921 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 912 921 912 921 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 930 934 930 934 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Kunisada1">[71]</xref>
###xml 974 976 974 976 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt</italic>
###xml 1038 1046 1038 1046 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 1242 1250 1242 1250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 756 771 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">transgenic mice</span>
There are several possible mechanisms by which ADAMTS20 could regulate Kit signaling. ADAMTS20 could be required directly for cleavage of either Kit and/or Kitl to produce sKitl. For example, the ADAM family member ADAM17 (GeneID: 11491) cleaves Kit in vitro, and ADAM17, 19 (GeneID: 8728) and 33 (GeneID: 110751) cleave Kitl [66]-[69]. However, sKitl did not rescue the melanoblast defect in bt9J/bt9J skin cultures as would be expected if Kitl were an essential substrate of ADAMTS20. As further evidence that the bt phenotype is not due to defective Kitl cleavage, bt9J/bt9J exhibited similar genetic interactions with both a Kitl null allele and with KitLSl-d/+ animals, which produce a short sKitl [42],[43],[70]. Kunisada et. al have also shown that transgenic mice over-expressing Kitl transgene, which greatly reduces the white spotting associated with Kit mutants, only slightly reduces the spotting in bt9J/bt9J animals [71]. Taken together this suggests that the bt phenotype is not due to defective cleavage of Kitl. Instead, Adamts20 may regulate the interaction of Kitl with Kit, the activation of Kit, or signaling downstream of the receptor. Future biochemical studies will be necessary to define the exact mechanism by which Adamts20 modulates Kit signaling.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 39 41 39 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 44 46 44 46 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 37 46 37 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 226 234 226 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 327 335 327 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
The observation that melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J trunk explants did not exhibit any response to soluble Kitl indicates that Kit signaling is defective, but it is important to note that this does not exclude the possibility that Adamts20 may additionally regulate other factors essential for melanoblast development. For example, Adamts20 could be required to activate other pathways that act synergistically with Kit to regulate melanoblast survival.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
###xml 21 23 21 23 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 26 28 26 28 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 19 28 19 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 29 33 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
ECM Alterations in bt9J/bt9J Mice
###end title 79
###begin p 80
###xml 36 44 36 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 157 166 157 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
###xml 241 249 241 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican</italic>
###xml 251 260 251 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20,</italic>
###xml 265 269 265 269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl</italic>
###xml 369 373 369 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 374 378 374 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Matsui1">[24]</xref>
###xml 379 383 379 383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-WehrleHaller4">[72]</xref>
###xml 565 569 565 569 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Takano1">[73]</xref>
###xml 633 635 633 635 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 638 640 638 640 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 631 640 631 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup>/bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
Another possible mechanism by which Adamts20 could modulate survival is by altering the extracellular matrix in which melanoblasts are located. We show that bt9J/bt9J mutants exhibit reduced cleavage of at least one ECM component, versican. Versican, Adamts20, and Kitl are expressed in embryonic skin at appropriate times and sites to regulate melanoblast development [12],[24],[72]. In fact, sKitl enhances melanoblast proliferation to a greater extent when primary NC cells are cultured on chondroitin sulfate, suggesting that the ECM can modulate Kit signaling [73]. Taken in context of this study, it could be melanoblasts in bt9J/bt9J explant cultures did not respond to sKitl because the ECM was defective.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 296 300 296 300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Schlessinger1">[74]</xref>
###xml 356 364 356 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS10</italic>
###xml 485 488 482 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Dagoneau1">[9]</xref>
###xml 607 611 604 608 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hirose1">[75]</xref>
###xml 612 616 609 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zou2">[77]</xref>
Versican proteolysis could influence melanoblast behavior and Kit signaling by promoting direct interactions of Kitl with Kit receptor. Such a scenario is analogous to heparin sulfate proteoglycans, which modulate growth factor signaling by sequestering ligand and promoting its receptor binding [74]. Studies of Weill-Marchesani syndrome strongly suggest ADAMTS10 (GeneID: 81794) regulates TGF betasignaling through its interactions with the ECM component, fibrillin-1 (GeneID: 2200) [9]. Interestingly, versican binds extracellular cytokines, including the secreted growth factor, midkine (GeneID: 17242) [75]-[77]. Future studies will reveal if versican, Kit, and Kitl physically interact and if versican regulates Kit signaling directly.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 134 145 134 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican V1</italic>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bad</italic>
###xml 259 263 259 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Sheng1">[78]</xref>
###xml 435 439 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wu2">[79]</xref>
###xml 440 444 437 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Wu3">[80]</xref>
###xml 492 496 489 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Haass1">[81]</xref>
###xml 497 501 494 498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zambruno1">[82]</xref>
###xml 631 639 628 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">versican</italic>
###xml 682 686 679 683 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Mjaatvedt1">[83]</xref>
###xml 710 718 707 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">versican</italic>
###xml 863 871 860 868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">versican</italic>
Versican and its proteolytic products could also promote melanoblast survival through a pathway that is independent of Kit signaling. Versican V1 promotes survival of NIH3T3 cells and down-regulates expression of the pro-apoptotic protein Bad (GeneID: 12015) [78]. Expression of the versican G1 domain protects sarcoma cells from apoptosis, and binding of the versican G3 domain to beta-Integrin promotes survival of astrocytoma cells [79],[80]. Since integrins are expressed by melanoblasts [81],[82], versican-integrin interactions are another potential mechanism by which versican could influence melanoblast development. Since versican mutants are embryonic lethal around E10.5 [83], conditional models of versican as well as transgenic animals containing constitutively cleaved and uncleaved Versican molecules will be necessary to assess the requirement of versican for melanoblast development.
###end p 82
###begin title 83
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS20</italic>
###xml 13 18 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
ADAMTS20 and Human Disease
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 75 82 75 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS9</italic>
###xml 87 95 87 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS20</italic>
###xml 152 160 152 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS20</italic>
###xml 278 282 278 282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Llamazares1">[84]</xref>
###xml 318 323 318 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAM9</italic>
###xml 343 351 343 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADAMTS13</italic>
###xml 436 440 436 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Cal1">[85]</xref>
###xml 441 445 441 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Zigrino1">[86]</xref>
###xml 462 470 462 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">VERSICAN</italic>
###xml 475 479 475 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KITL</italic>
###xml 576 580 576 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Domenzain1">[87]</xref>
###xml 581 585 581 585 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Touab2">[91]</xref>
###xml 612 620 612 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
Given that cell survival is an integral component of melanoma progression, ADAMTS9 and ADAMTS20 are excellent candidates for participating in melanoma. ADAMTS20 over-expression has not been carefully examined in melanoma, but has been observed in brain, colon and breast tumors [47],[84]. The related metalloproteases ADAM9 (GeneID: 8754) and ADAMTS13 are upregulated in primary melanoma tumors and in melanoma cell lines, respectively [85],[86]. Interestingly, VERSICAN and KITL overexpression are observed in primary melanomas and levels correlate with melanoma progression [87]-[91]. Given the requirement of Adamts20 for Kit signaling and versican cleavage, it is intriguing to consider how dysregulation of signaling between ADAMTS20, Kit, and versican might contribute to melanoma progression.
###end p 84
###begin title 85
Materials and Methods
###end title 85
###begin title 86
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Mice and Genetic Interactions
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 69 76 69 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt-Bei1</sup>
###xml 61 76 61 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20<sup>bt-Bei1</sup></italic>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt9J</sup>
###xml 116 128 116 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20<sup>bt9J</sup></italic>
###xml 168 172 168 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct-</italic>
###xml 180 182 180 182 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mi</sup>
###xml 187 193 187 193 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tm1Alf</sup>
###xml 178 193 178 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mi<sup>Mi</sup>, Kit<sup>tm1Alf</sup></italic>
###xml 199 201 199 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sl</sup>
###xml 195 201 195 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kitl<sup>Sl</sup></italic>
###xml 231 235 231 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sl-d</sup>
###xml 228 235 228 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kit<sup>Sl-d</sup></italic>
###xml 283 285 283 285 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 276 285 276 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9<sup>ko</sup></italic>
###xml 297 299 297 299 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ko</sup>
###xml 297 299 297 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>ko</sup></italic>
###xml 14 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The following mouse stocks were used and kindly provided by: Adamts20bt-Bei1 (David Beier, Harvard Medical School), Adamts20bt9J (Lynn Lamoreux, Texas A&M University), Dct-LacZ, MiMi, Kittm1Alf, KitlSl (Heinz Arnheiter, NINDS), KitSl-d (Jackson Laboratories, Bar Harbor, ME). Adamts9ko and Adamts5ko knockout animals (both on a C57Bl/6 background) are described elsewhere (D. McCullough, H. Enomoto, S. Apte, unpublished). Quantification of white spotting was performed using Image J software () (NIH, Bethesda, MD) and statistical significance of spotting calculated using ANOVA tests.
###end p 87
###begin title 88
Genotyping and Sequencing
###end title 88
###begin p 89
###xml 57 61 57 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt9J</sup>
###xml 49 61 49 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20<sup>bt9J</sup></italic>
###xml 144 146 144 146 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 865 889 847 871 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">TTCAGCACAGCTATTCTGGAAGAC</named-content>
###xml 908 929 890 911 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">GCACCTGAGGCAGACATACAC</named-content>
###xml 948 966 930 948 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">CTTACCGAGATAGTTGTC</named-content>
###xml 1000 1018 982 1000 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">CTTACCGAAATAGTTGTC</named-content>
###xml 1033 1035 1015 1017 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9J</sup>
###xml 1031 1035 1013 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt<sup>9J</sup></italic>
cDNA was sequenced by GeneDx (Gaithersburg, MD). Adamts20bt9J animals were genotyped using standard conditions on an ABIPrism7000 using a TaqmanTM assay of genomic DNA. For this assay, a region containing the point mutation is amplified by PCR. Two fluorescently labeled single-stranded oligonucleotides (probes), one complementary to the wild-type product, and one complementary to the mutant product are included in the assay. The relative amount of wild-type and mutant product is measured by fluorescence quenched upon DNA synthesis. Allelic discrimination was performed to detect the total levels of each allele at the conclusion of the PCR reaction. The following cycling conditions were used: 1. 95degreesC for 10 minutes 1x, 2. 92degreesC for 15 seconds, 3. 55degreesC for 60 seconds (2 and 3 repeated 40 times). The following primers and probes were used: TTCAGCACAGCTATTCTGGAAGAC (forward primer), GCACCTGAGGCAGACATACAC (reverse primer), CTTACCGAGATAGTTGTC (VIC probe, C57BL/6 allele), and CTTACCGAAATAGTTGTC (FAM probe, bt9J allele) (designed using Applied Biosystems software, Foster City, CA).
###end p 89
###begin title 90
Melanoblast Quantitation
###end title 90
###begin p 91
###xml 211 214 211 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dct</italic>
For quantitation of whole mount embryos, melanoblasts were counted from both sides of each embryo within a 1 mmx0.7 mm field surrounding the eye or the trunk. For quantitation of melanoblasts in E13.5 sections, Dct-LacZ expression was scored. The mitotic index was calculated using the average number of PH3+ melanoblasts per section divided by the average number of total melanoblasts per section and multiplied by 100. The apoptotic index was calculated using the average number of CC3+ melanoblasts per section divided by the average number of total melanoblasts per section and multiplied by 100. For quantitation of melanoblasts in different skin compartments the following criteria were used: melanoblasts above the basal membrane were classified as epidermal, melanoblasts below the basal membrane were classified as dermal, and melanoblasts crossing the basal membrane and present in both regions were classified as dermal/epidermal region. The following statistical tests were used: for average number of melanoblasts in sections and whole mount embryos (two-tailed Student's t-test), for proportion of total melanoblasts and apoptotic melanoblasts in skin layers (Chi-square test of independence), for proportion of proliferating and apoptotic melanoblasts (Fisher's test).
###end p 91
###begin title 92
###xml 44 51 41 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In situ</italic>
Whole Mount beta-Galactosidase Staining and In situ Hybridization
###end title 92
###begin p 93
###xml 75 79 72 76 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hou1">[41]</xref>
###xml 81 88 78 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In situ</italic>
###xml 141 145 138 142 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Baxter2">[92]</xref>
###xml 165 173 162 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 180 184 177 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Rao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 201 212 198 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican V1</italic>
###xml 236 247 233 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Versican V1</italic>
###xml 290 296 287 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pmel17</italic>
###xml 332 336 329 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Baxter2">[92]</xref>
###xml 355 362 352 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 369 373 366 370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Jungers1">[58]</xref>
###xml 159 164 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 195 200 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 230 235 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 349 354 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
beta-galactosidase activity staining was performed as previously described [41]. In situ hybridization was performed as previously described [92] using a 1 Kb mouse Adamts20 probe [12], a 644 bp mouse Versican V1 probe made using mouse Versican V1 cDNA (a kind gift of Andrew Copp, UCL), a Pmel17 probe made as previously described [92], and a 1 Kb mouse Adamts9 probe [58].
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Immunofluorescence
###end title 94
###begin p 95
###xml 321 326 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 376 382 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 437 443 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 514 520 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 570 576 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 642 647 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 657 663 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Frozen sections were prepared from embryos fixed overnight in 4% paraformaldehyde. Staining was performed with modifications to manufacturer's protocol (Vector Laboratories, Burlingame, CA), and sections were mounted using Hardset Vectashield with DAPI (Vector Laboratories). The following antibodies were used at 1:200: mouse anti- beta galactosidase (Promega, Madison, WI), rabbit anti-cleaved Caspase-3 (Cell Signaling, Danvers, MA), rabbit anti-phospho-Histone H3 (Upstate Biotechnology, Charlottesville, VA), rabbit anti-versican GAG beta (Chemicon, Temecula, CA), rabbit anti-versican V0/V1 Neo (Affinity Bioreagents, Golden, CO), anti-mouse and anti-rabbit rhodamine-conjugated or FITC-conjugated secondary antibodies (Vector Laboratories).
###end p 95
###begin title 96
Generation of Expression Plasmids and Versican Digestion
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts20</italic>
###xml 209 216 209 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adamts9</italic>
###xml 242 246 242 246 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 336 340 336 340 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Somerville1">[47]</xref>
###xml 60 65 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 901 906 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 935 941 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 975 981 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1021 1026 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1110 1116 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1130 1135 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Adamts20 short isoform cDNA was assembled by PCR from E17.5 mouse embryo mRNA, sequence verified, and cloned into pcDNAmyc-hisA+ plasmid (Invitrogen, Thousand Oaks, CA). The expression plasmid for full-length Adamts9 was previously described [47]. Transfected or untransfected cells were incubated with versican as previously described [47]. Extracts of embryo skin were prepared using a RIPA lysis buffer containing protease inhibitor mixture (20 microl) and 2 mM phenylmethylsulphonyl fluoride (Pierce, Rockford, IL). For analysis of total versican, cell extracts were treated with 0.1 units chondroitinase ABC (Associates of Cape Cod, East Falmouth, MA) in 0.1 M Tris, 50 mM NaAc for 10 minutes at 37degreesC. Skin extracts and conditioned medium from transfected cells were run on 4-12% SDS-Polyacrylamide gels (Invitrogen) and analyzed by Western blotting using the following primary antibodies: mouse anti-myc 9E10 (Invitrogen), rabbit anti-versican GAG betaat 1:1000, rabbit anti-versican V0/V1 Neo at 1:1000, and mouse anti-alpha-Tubulin at 1:1000 (Sigma, St.Louis, MO); and secondary antibodies: anti-rabbit HRP and anti-mouse HRP (Amersham, Piscataway, NJ).
###end p 97
###begin title 98
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ex vivo</italic>
Ex vivo Embryonic Skin Analysis
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 70 79 70 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/+;Dct-</italic>
###xml 88 98 88 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bt/bt;Dct-</italic>
###xml 781 785 774 778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000003-Hou1">[41]</xref>
Dorsal skin between the forelimb and hindlimb was isolated from E13.5 bt/+;Dct-LacZ and bt/bt;Dct-LacZ embryos with ventral tissue portions and internal organs removed. The skin explants were placed epidermal side up onto polyethylene terepthlate track-etched membranes in a cell culture insert (8.0 microm pore size, Becton-Dickinson, Franklin Lakes, NJ). Separate cultures were established for each explant. Explants were cultured for four days with 95% DMEM, 5% FBS (control medium) and as noted the medium was supplemented daily with 500 ng/ml Kitl (R&D Systems, Minneapolis, MN). After a culture period of four days, the explants were fixed in 4% paraformaldehyde in PBS (pH 7.4) for one hour and staining for beta-galactosidase activity was performed as previously described [41].
###end p 99
###begin title 100
Newborn Skin Analysis
###end title 100
###begin p 101
Skin was removed from newborn pups, fixed in 4% paraformaldehyde overnight and washed 3x in PBS and then analyzed on the dermal side for pigmentation. Pigmentation was scored as the extent of pigmentation between anterior and posterior edges of samples, using the following scale: 1 (no pigmentation), 2 (between 0 and 25%), 3 (between 25 and 50%), 4 (between 50 and 75%), 5 (between 75% and 100%). Statistical significance was calculated using a student's t test.
###end p 101

###begin p 109
Kit heterozygous mutations do not exacerbate the bt phenotype at E12.5. Representative images of the trunks of E12.5 bt9J/+;Kittm1Alf/+ (A) and bt9J/bt9J;Kittm1Alf/+ embryos (B) (n = 6 each genotype).
